## Codex <sup>4/25/2026, 2:58:14 PM</sup>

A solid starting point for this app is a feature-first Clean Architecture layout, with shared app-wide code separated into `core` and `services`.

```text
lib/

│   │

```

**Why this structure**

`features/` is the center of the app because your business logic is feature-driven: expenses, subscriptions, dashboard, insights. This keeps each module isolated, easier to test, and easier to scale when the app grows.

`presentation / domain / data` inside each feature works well here because:
- `presentation` handles UI and Cubit only
- `domain` stays pure and contains business rules
- `data` handles Hive, Firebase, models, and repository implementations

This separation matters for your offline-first requirement. Since local storage is the source of truth:
- `data/datasources/local_*` is always primary
- `data/datasources/remote_*` is optional and sync-only
- `domain` does not care whether data came from Hive or Firestore
- `presentation` only talks to use cases or Cubit, never directly to Hive/Firebase

**Why `core` and `services` are separate**

`core/` is for reusable app-wide pieces that should not belong to a single feature, like errors, constants, shared widgets, and base use case classes.

`services/` is for infrastructure setup:
- Hive initialization
- Firebase setup
- notification handling

This prevents low-level platform/service code from leaking into feature modules.

**Why this is good for production**

- Easy to add new features without touching unrelated code
- Easier unit testing because repositories and use cases are isolated
- Safer refactoring because dependencies flow inward
- Better long-term maintainability than grouping by `screens`, `models`, and `widgets` globally

**Important design choices for this app**

- Hive should back all core app operations
- Firestore should only mirror/sync selected data
- Repository interfaces should live in `domain`, implementations in `data`
- Dashboard and insights can read from local repositories, not directly from Hive boxes
- Notifications should be triggered from subscription logic, but managed by a dedicated service

Next, I can move to step 2 and define the core domain models for `Expense`, `Category`, and `Subscription` in a clean, scalable way.

## Codex <sup>4/25/2026, 3:15:04 PM</sup>

It’s okay if your `core/` folder is acting as the app-wide shared layer, but I’d be a bit selective about what goes there.

`themes` inside `core` is perfectly fine. Shared styling is cross-cutting and belongs there naturally.

`di` is also acceptable inside `core` in many projects, especially if you treat it as infrastructure wiring for the whole app. Some teams keep it as top-level `di/` just to make bootstrap code easier to find, but either approach is fine.

`services` inside `core` can also work, but only for truly shared infrastructure services like local notifications, connectivity, storage setup, or Firebase wrappers. If `services` starts holding feature-specific logic, `core` becomes a dumping ground, which is the real problem.

`routes` is the one I’d usually avoid burying in `core` unless your routing is purely global app configuration. Routing is closer to app composition than “core business support,” so I prefer `app/routes/` or `presentation/routes/`.

So the short version is:

- `core/themes`: good
- `core/di`: good enough
- `core/services`: good if they are shared infra services
- `core/routes`: workable, but `app/routes` is usually cleaner

The issue is not “can it live in `core`?” The issue is whether `core` stays small, generic, and reusable instead of becoming a miscellaneous folder.

A practical rule:
- Put it in `core` if multiple features depend on it and it contains no feature-specific business logic.
- Put it in `app` if it wires the application together.
- Put it in a feature if it mainly serves one feature.

If you want, I can give you a refined folder structure version that keeps your preferred `core/` style while still staying clean and production-ready.

I created the expense domain layer under [`lib/features/expenses/domain/entities/expense.dart`](d:/Dev/FlutterProjects/spend_wise/lib/features/expenses/domain/entities/expense.dart), [`repositories/expense_repository.dart`](d:/Dev/FlutterProjects/spend_wise/lib/features/expenses/domain/repositories/expense_repository.dart), and the two use cases in [`usecases/add_expense.dart`](d:/Dev/FlutterProjects/spend_wise/lib/features/expenses/domain/usecases/add_expense.dart) and [`usecases/get_expenses.dart`](d:/Dev/FlutterProjects/spend_wise/lib/features/expenses/domain/usecases/get_expenses.dart).

The decisions are intentionally minimal and production-friendly:
- `Expense` is a pure Dart entity with no package dependencies, so the domain layer stays independent from Flutter, Hive, Firebase, or serialization details.
- The entity contains only business-relevant fields: `id`, `title`, `amount`, `categoryId`, `date`, and optional `note`. That keeps it stable while leaving persistence concerns for the data layer.
- `ExpenseRepository` is an abstract contract in the domain layer, which lets the app depend on behavior, not on Hive or Firestore implementations.
- `AddExpense` and `GetExpenses` each do one thing. This keeps Cubits simple later and makes testing straightforward.

A couple of small best-practice touches are already included:
- `Expense` is immutable with `final` fields and a `const` constructor.
- There’s an assertion preventing negative amounts.
- Manual equality and `hashCode` are implemented without external dependencies.
- `copyWith` is included because it becomes useful quickly for edit flows and state updates.

One note on scope: `GetExpenses` currently returns `Future<List<Expense>>`, which is a good starting point for CRUD. Later, if you want the UI to react live to Hive changes, we can add a separate `WatchExpenses` use case instead of overloading this one.

Next step can be the `data` layer for expenses:
- `ExpenseModel`
- Hive adapter mapping
- local data source
- repository implementation

```
import 'package:hive/hive.dart';

import '../models/expense_model.dart';

abstract class ExpenseLocalDataSource {
  Future<void> addExpense(ExpenseModel expense);

  Future<List<ExpenseModel>> getExpenses();
}

class HiveExpenseLocalDataSource implements ExpenseLocalDataSource {
  HiveExpenseLocalDataSource(this._box);

  static const String boxName = 'expenses_box';

  final Box<Map<dynamic, dynamic>> _box;

  @override
  Future<void> addExpense(ExpenseModel expense) async {
    await _box.put(expense.id, expense.toJson());
  }

  @override
  Future<List<ExpenseModel>> getExpenses() async {
    return _box.values
        .map(
          (expenseMap) => ExpenseModel.fromJson(
            Map<String, dynamic>.from(expenseMap),
          ),
        )
        .toList(growable: false);
  }
}
```

</details>

```
import '../../domain/entities/expense.dart';
import '../../domain/repositories/expense_repository.dart';
import '../datasources/expense_local_data_source.dart';
import '../models/expense_model.dart';

class ExpenseRepositoryImpl implements ExpenseRepository {
  const ExpenseRepositoryImpl(this._localDataSource);

  final ExpenseLocalDataSource _localDataSource;

  @override
  Future<void> addExpense(Expense expense) {
    final expenseModel = ExpenseModel.fromEntity(expense);
    return _localDataSource.addExpense(expenseModel);
  }

  @override
  Future<List<Expense>> getExpenses() async {
    final expenseModels = await _localDataSource.getExpenses();
    return expenseModels.map((expenseModel) => expenseModel.toEntity()).toList(
          growable: false,
        );
  }
}
```

---

## Codex <sup>4/27/2026, 3:32:09 PM</sup>

I implemented the `expenses` data layer and connected it to the domain layer.

What was added:
- [`ExpenseModel`](d:/Dev/FlutterProjects/spend_wise/lib/features/expenses/data/models/expense_model.dart) with `json_serializable` structure
- [`expense_model.g.dart`](d:/Dev/FlutterProjects/spend_wise/lib/features/expenses/data/models/expense_model.g.dart) containing the JSON mapping functions
- [`ExpenseLocalDataSource`](d:/Dev/FlutterProjects/spend_wise/lib/features/expenses/data/datasources/expense_local_data_source.dart) and `HiveExpenseLocalDataSource`
- [`ExpenseRepositoryImpl`](d:/Dev/FlutterProjects/spend_wise/lib/features/expenses/data/repositories/expense_repository_impl.dart)

How it works:
- `ExpenseModel` is the data-layer representation of `Expense`
- `ExpenseModel.fromEntity()` converts domain `Expense` into a storable model
- `toEntity()` converts stored model data back into the domain entity
- `HiveExpenseLocalDataSource` stores expenses in a Hive box using the expense `id` as the key
- `ExpenseRepositoryImpl` implements the domain `ExpenseRepository` and delegates persistence to the local data source

I also updated [`pubspec.yaml`](d:/Dev/FlutterProjects/spend_wise/pubspec.yaml) to add:
- `hive`
- `json_annotation`
- `build_runner`
- `json_serializable`

Why this structure:
- The domain layer stays clean and independent
- Hive remains the local source of truth
- JSON serialization is isolated in the model, not the entity
- The repository is the bridge between domain and data, which keeps Cubit and UI unaware of storage details

One important note: I did not complete dependency installation or run code generation through Flutter tooling in this session, so `flutter pub get` still needs to be run locally before analysis/build.

```
import '../../domain/entities/expense.dart';
import '../../../../core/base/requests_status.dart';

class ExpenseState {
  const ExpenseState({
    this.status = RequestsStatus.initial,
    this.expenses = const [],
    this.errorMessage,
  });

  final RequestsStatus status;
  final List<Expense> expenses;
  final String? errorMessage;

  ExpenseState copyWith({
    RequestsStatus? status,
    List<Expense>? expenses,
    String? errorMessage,
    bool clearErrorMessage = false,
  }) {
    return ExpenseState(
      status: status ?? this.status,
      expenses: expenses ?? this.expenses,
      errorMessage:
          clearErrorMessage ? null : (errorMessage ?? this.errorMessage),
    );
  }
}
```

</details>

<details>
<summary>Result</summary>

```
Exit code: 0
Wall time: 0.3 seconds
Output:
import 'package:flutter_bloc/flutter_bloc.dart';

import '../../../../core/base/requests_status.dart';
import '../../domain/entities/expense.dart';
import '../../domain/usecases/add_expense.dart';
import '../../domain/usecases/get_expenses.dart';
import 'expense_state.dart';

class ExpenseCubit extends Cubit<ExpenseState> {
  ExpenseCubit({
    required AddExpense addExpense,
    required GetExpenses getExpenses,
  })  : _addExpense = addExpense,
        _getExpenses = getExpenses,
        super(const ExpenseState());

  final AddExpense _addExpense;
  final GetExpenses _getExpenses;

  Future<void> loadExpenses() async {
    emit(
      state.copyWith(
        status: RequestsStatus.loading,
        clearErrorMessage: true,
      ),
    );

    try {
      final expenses = await _getExpenses();
      emit(
        state.copyWith(
          status: RequestsStatus.success,
          expenses: expenses,
        
...(truncated)
```

</details>

I created the expense presentation state management layer with:
- [`RequestsStatus`](d:/Dev/FlutterProjects/spend_wise/lib/core/base/requests_status.dart)
- [`ExpenseState`](d:/Dev/FlutterProjects/spend_wise/lib/features/expenses/presentation/cubit/expense_state.dart)
- [`ExpenseCubit`](d:/Dev/FlutterProjects/spend_wise/lib/features/expenses/presentation/cubit/expense_cubit.dart)

I also added `flutter_bloc` to [`pubspec.yaml`](d:/Dev/FlutterProjects/spend_wise/pubspec.yaml).

Why it’s structured this way:
- `ExpenseCubit` depends only on `AddExpense` and `GetExpenses`, so the UI stays separated from repositories and Hive.
- `ExpenseState` holds only UI-relevant state: `status`, `expenses`, and `errorMessage`.
- `RequestsStatus` gives a simple and reusable way to represent `initial`, `loading`, `success`, and `error` without overengineering.

Behavior:
- `loadExpenses()` emits `loading`, then either `success` with the list or `error`.
- `addExpense()` emits `loading`, saves through `AddExpense`, reloads through `GetExpenses`, then emits `success` or `error`.
- `ExpenseState.copyWith()` supports clean state updates and includes `clearErrorMessage` so stale errors don’t linger.

One important note: I haven’t run `flutter pub get` or analyzer here, so dependency resolution still needs to be done locally before build/test.

If you want, the next clean step is building the first expenses UI screen and wiring this Cubit into it.

I added a complete first-pass UI flow for expenses and connected it to `ExpenseCubit`.

What’s included:
- [`main.dart`](d:/Dev/FlutterProjects/spend_wise/lib/main.dart): initializes Hive, creates the local data source, repository, use cases, and provides `ExpenseCubit`
- [`ExpensesPage`](d:/Dev/FlutterProjects/spend_wise/lib/features/expenses/presentation/pages/expenses_page.dart): shows loading, empty, error, and populated list states
- [`AddExpensePage`](d:/Dev/FlutterProjects/spend_wise/lib/features/expenses/presentation/pages/add_expense_page.dart): form for title, amount, category, date, and note
- [`ExpenseListItem`](d:/Dev/FlutterProjects/spend_wise/lib/features/expenses/presentation/widgets/expense_list_item.dart): reusable card UI for each expense

A couple of implementation choices were deliberate:
- The UI talks only to `ExpenseCubit`, not directly to Hive or the repository, which keeps presentation clean.
- The layout uses `LayoutBuilder`, constrained width, and adaptive padding so it stays neat on both phones and larger screens.
- The add screen now only closes when the Cubit reports success; if saving fails, it stays open and shows an error snackbar.

I also updated dependencies in [`pubspec.yaml`](d:/Dev/FlutterProjects/spend_wise/pubspec.yaml) to include `flutter_bloc` and `hive_flutter`, and I aligned the Hive box typing in the local data source.

I wasn’t able to run `flutter pub get` or a full compile check here, so that still needs to be done locally before build/testing.

```
Output:
import 'package:hive/hive.dart';

import '../models/expense_model.dart';

abstract class ExpenseLocalDataSource {
  Future<void> addExpense(ExpenseModel expense);

  Future<List<ExpenseModel>> getExpenses();
}

class HiveExpenseLocalDataSource implements ExpenseLocalDataSource {
  HiveExpenseLocalDataSource(this._box);

  static const String boxName = 'expenses_box';

  final Box<Map> _box;

  @override
  Future<void> addExpense(ExpenseModel expense) async {
    await _box.put(expense.id, expense.toJson());
  }

  @override
  Future<List<ExpenseModel>> getExpenses() async {
    return _box.values
        .map(
          (expenseMap) => ExpenseModel.fromJson(
            Map<String, dynamic>.from(expenseMap),
          ),
        )
        .toList(growable: false);
  }
}
```

</details>

I set up dependency injection for the expenses feature using `GetIt` and moved the manual wiring out of `main.dart`.

What changed:
- Added [`lib/di/injection_container.dart`](d:/Dev/FlutterProjects/spend_wise/lib/di/injection_container.dart)
- Updated [`lib/main.dart`](d:/Dev/FlutterProjects/spend_wise/lib/main.dart) to call `setupDependencies()` and resolve `ExpenseCubit` from DI
- Added `get_it` in [`pubspec.yaml`](d:/Dev/FlutterProjects/spend_wise/pubspec.yaml)

What’s registered:
- Hive box: `Box<Map>` registered as a singleton using the expenses box name as `instanceName`
- Local data source: `ExpenseLocalDataSource` as `LazySingleton`
- Repository: `ExpenseRepository` as `LazySingleton`
- Use cases: `AddExpense` and `GetExpenses` as `LazySingleton`
- Cubit: `ExpenseCubit` as `Factory`

Why these lifetimes:
- Hive box is a singleton because the opened box should be shared app-wide.
- Repository and use cases are lazy singletons because they are stateless and reusable.
- Cubit is a factory because UI state objects should be created per screen lifecycle, not shared globally.

Why this is better:
- `main.dart` is now only responsible for app bootstrap.
- Presentation no longer knows how repositories or Hive are constructed.
- The expenses feature is easier to test because dependencies can be swapped cleanly.
- This scales well when you add categories, subscriptions, sync, and notifications later.

One note: I didn’t run `flutter pub get` or compile checks here, so dependency resolution still needs to be run locally.

import 'package:flutter/material.dart';
import 'package:flutter_bloc/flutter_bloc.dart';

import '../../../../core/base/requests_status.dart';
import '../../domain/entities/expense.dart';
import '../cubit/expense_cubit.dart';

class AddExpensePage extends StatefulWidget {
  const AddExpensePage({super.key});

  @override
  State<AddExpensePage> createState() => _AddExpensePageState();
}

class _AddExpensePageState extends State<AddExpensePage> {
  final _formKey = GlobalKey<FormState>();
  final _titleController = TextEditingController();
  final _amountController = TextEditingController();
  final _categoryController = TextEditingController();
  final _noteController = TextEditingController();

  DateTime _selectedDate = DateTime.now();
  bool _isSubmitting = false;

  @override
  void dispose() {
    _titleController.dispose();
    _amountController.dispose();
    _categoryController.dispose();
    _noteController.dispose();
    super.dispose();
  }

  Future<void> _pickDate() async {
    final pickedDate = await showDatePicker(
      context: context,
      initialDate: _selectedDate,
      firstDate: DateTime(2020),
      lastDate: DateTime(2100),
    );

    if (pickedDate != null) {
      setState(() {
        _selectedDate = pickedDate;
      });
    }
  }

  Future<void> _submit() async {
    final isValid = _formKey.currentState?.validate() ?? false;
    if (!isValid || _isSubmitting) {
      return;
    }

    setState(() {
      _isSubmitting = true;
    });

    final expense = Expense(
      id: DateTime.now().microsecondsSinceEpoch.toString(),
      title: _titleController.text.trim(),
      amount: double.parse(_amountController.text.trim()),
      categoryId: _categoryController.text.trim(),
      date: _selectedDate,
      note: _noteController.text.trim().isEmpty
          ? null
          : _noteController.text.trim(),
    );

    await context.read<ExpenseCubit>().addExpense(expense);

    if (!mounted) {
      return;
    }

    final state = context.read<ExpenseCubit>().state;

    setState(() {
      _isSubmitting = false;
    });

    if (state.status == RequestsStatus.success) {
      Navigator.of(context).pop();
      return;
    }

    final errorMessage = state.errorMessage ?? 'Failed to save expense.';
    ScaffoldMessenger.of(
      context,
    ).showSnackBar(SnackBar(content: Text(errorMessage)));
  }

  @override
  Widget build(BuildContext context) {
    final textTheme = Theme.of(context).textTheme;

    return Scaffold(
      appBar: AppBar(title: const Text('Add Expense')),
      body: SafeArea(
        child: LayoutBuilder(
          builder: (context, constraints) {
            final horizontalPadding = constraints.maxWidth >= 700 ? 24.0 : 16.0;

            return Align(
              alignment: Alignment.topCenter,
              child: ConstrainedBox(
                constraints: const BoxConstraints(maxWidth: 720),
                child: SingleChildScrollView(
                  padding: EdgeInsets.all(horizontalPadding),
                  child: Form(
                    key: _formKey,
                    child: Column(
                      crossAxisAlignment: CrossAxisAlignment.start,
                      children: [
                        Text(
                          'Track a new expense',
                          style: textTheme.headlineSmall,
                        ),
                        const SizedBox(height: 8),
                        Text(
                          'Keep it simple for now. We can replace the category field with a picker once categories are built.',
                          style: textTheme.bodyMedium,
                        ),
                        const SizedBox(height: 24),
                        TextFormField(
                          controller: _titleController,
                          textInputAction: TextInputAction.next,
                          decoration: const InputDecoration(
                            labelText: 'Title',
                            hintText: 'Groceries',
                          ),
                          validator: (value) {
                            if (value == null || value.trim().isEmpty) {
                              return 'Title is required.';
                            }

                            return null;
                          },
                        ),
                        const SizedBox(height: 16),
                        TextFormField(
                          controller: _amountController,
                          keyboardType: const TextInputType.numberWithOptions(
                            decimal: true,
                          ),
                          textInputAction: TextInputAction.next,
                          decoration: const InputDecoration(
                            labelText: 'Amount',
                            hintText: '24.99',
                            prefixText: '\$ ',
                          ),
                          validator: (value) {
                            final amount = double.tryParse(value?.trim() ?? '');
                            if (amount == null || amount <= 0) {
                              return 'Enter a valid amount.';
                            }

                            return null;
                          },
                        ),
                        const SizedBox(height: 16),
                        TextFormField(
                          controller: _categoryController,
                          textInputAction: TextInputAction.next,
                          decoration: const InputDecoration(
                            labelText: 'Category',
                            hintText: 'Food',
                          ),
                          validator: (value) {
                            if (value == null || value.trim().isEmpty) {
                              return 'Category is required.';
                            }

                            return null;
                          },
                        ),
                        const SizedBox(height: 16),
                        InkWell(
                          onTap: _pickDate,
                          borderRadius: BorderRadius.circular(12),
                          child: InputDecorator(
                            decoration: const InputDecoration(
                              labelText: 'Date',
                              suffixIcon: Icon(Icons.calendar_today_outlined),
                            ),
                            child: Text(_formatDate(_selectedDate)),
                          ),
                        ),
                        const SizedBox(height: 16),
                        TextFormField(
                          controller: _noteController,
                          minLines: 3,
                          maxLines: 5,
                          decoration: const InputDecoration(
                            labelText: 'Note',
                            hintText: 'Optional details',
                          ),
                        ),
                        const SizedBox(height: 28),
                        SizedBox(
                          width: double.infinity,
                          child: FilledButton(
                            onPressed: _isSubmitting ? null : _submit,
                            child: Padding(
                              padding: const EdgeInsets.symmetric(vertical: 14),
                              child: Text(
                                _isSubmitting ? 'Saving...' : 'Save expense',
                              ),
                            ),
                          ),
                        ),
                      ],
                    ),
                  ),
                ),
              ),
            );
          },
        ),
      ),
    );
  }

  String _formatDate(DateTime date) {
    final month = date.month.toString().padLeft(2, '0');
    final day = date.day.toString().padLeft(2, '0');
    return '${date.year}-$month-$day';
  }
}

```
class ExpenseCubit extends Cubit<ExpenseState> {
  ExpenseCubit({
    required AddExpense addExpense,
    required GetExpenses getExpenses,
  }) : _addExpense = addExpense,
       _getExpenses = getExpenses,
       super(const ExpenseState());

  final AddExpense _addExpense;
  final GetExpenses _getExpenses;

  Future<void> loadExpenses() async {
    emit(
      state.copyWith(status: RequestsStatus.loading, clearErrorMessage: true),
    );

    try {
      final expenses = await _getExpenses();
      emit(
        state.copyWith(
          status: RequestsStatus.success,
          expenses: expenses,
          clearErrorMessage: true,
```

```
import '../../domain/entities/expense.dart';
import '../../../../core/base/requests_status.dart';

class ExpenseState {
  const ExpenseState({
    this.status = RequestsStatus.initial,
    this.expenses = const [],
    this.errorMessage,
  });

  final RequestsStatus status;
  final List<Expense> expenses;
  final String? errorMessage;

  ExpenseState copyWith({
    RequestsStatus? status,
    List<Expense>? expenses,
    String? errorMessage,
    bool clearErrorMessage = false,
  }) {
    return ExpenseState(
      status: status ?? this.status,
      expenses: expenses ?? this.expenses,
      errorMessage: clearErrorMessage
          ? null
          : (errorMessage ?? this.errorMessage),
    );
  }
}
```

```
      case RouteNames.expensePage:
```

I’m on the UI refactor step now. The plan is:
- Add `ScreenUtilInit` at the app root.
- Make `AddExpensePage` stateless with `BlocListener` + `BlocBuilder`.

```
class AppRouters {
  Route? onGenerateRoute(RouteSettings settings) {
    switch (settings.name) {
      case RouteNames.expensePage:
        return MaterialPageRoute(builder: (_) => const ExpensesPage());
      case RouteNames.addExpensePage:
        return MaterialPageRoute(builder: (_) => const AddExpensePage());
      default:
        return null;
    }
```

Refactored the add-expense flow so the page is mostly declarative and the Cubit owns form behavior.

What changed:
- [`AddExpensePage`](d:/Dev/FlutterProjects/spend_wise/lib/features/expenses/presentation/pages/add_expense_page.dart) is now a `StatelessWidget`
- Business state moved into [`ExpenseCubit`](d:/Dev/FlutterProjects/spend_wise/lib/features/expenses/presentation/cubit/expense_cubit.dart) and [`ExpenseState`](d:/Dev/FlutterProjects/spend_wise/lib/features/expenses/presentation/cubit/expense_state.dart)
- Extracted reusable widgets:
  - [`ExpenseTextField`](d:/Dev/FlutterProjects/spend_wise/lib/features/expenses/presentation/widgets/expense_text_field.dart)
  - [`ExpenseDatePicker`](d:/Dev/FlutterProjects/spend_wise/lib/features/expenses/presentation/widgets/expense_date_picker.dart)
  - [`ExpenseForm`](d:/Dev/FlutterProjects/spend_wise/lib/features/expenses/presentation/widgets/expense_form.dart)
- Integrated `flutter_screenutil` in [`SpendWiseApp`](d:/Dev/FlutterProjects/spend_wise/lib/spend_wise_app.dart) and replaced many fixed sizes with `.h`, `.w`, `.sp`
- Updated [`ExpensesPage`](d:/Dev/FlutterProjects/spend_wise/lib/features/expenses/presentation/pages/expenses_page.dart) and [`ExpenseListItem`](d:/Dev/FlutterProjects/spend_wise/lib/features/expenses/presentation/widgets/expense_list_item.dart) to use the new state model and responsive sizing

Why this improves the architecture:
- The page no longer owns submission state or selected date, so UI is thinner and easier to reason about.
- `ExpenseCubit` now manages:
  - expense list loading
  - form submission status
  - selected date
  - form reset behavior
- `BlocListener` handles side effects like navigation and snackbars.
- `BlocBuilder` handles rendering only.
- Controllers stay in the form widget, which is a good compromise: UI-only input state stays local, business workflow stays in Cubit.

Important state improvement:
- I split the old single `status` into `expensesStatus` and `submissionStatus`.
- This avoids a common bug where loading the form submission accidentally affects the list screen state.

Responsive UI:
- `ScreenUtilInit` is now set in the app root.
- The add form and expense list use `.h`, `.w`, `.sp` for padding, spacing, widths, and font sizes.

One small UX fix included:
- The form now clears only after a successful submission, not after a failed one.

I didn’t run `flutter pub get` or analyzer here, so you’ll still need to install the new dependency and run a compile check locally.

Refactored [`ExpensesPage`](d:/Dev/FlutterProjects/spend_wise/lib/features/expenses/presentation/pages/expenses_page.dart) into smaller, clearer pieces without changing the feature behavior.

What changed:
- Kept `ExpensesPage` focused on page-level scaffold only
- Moved body composition into `_ExpensesPageBody`
- Moved state branching into `_ExpensesStateView`
- Extracted list rendering into `_ExpensesListView`
- Renamed the empty/error widget to `_ExpensesFeedbackView`
- Centralized add-page navigation in `ExpensesPage._openAddExpensePage()`

Why this is better:
- The page is easier to read because layout, state branching, and list rendering are separated.
- Navigation logic is no longer duplicated between the FAB and empty state.
- The state view now expresses intent more clearly with `_isInitialLoading` and `_hasInitialLoadError`.
- The extracted list view stays strongly typed with `List<Expense>`, which keeps presentation aligned with the domain layer.

I didn’t change feature behavior, only structure and readability. If you want, the next good step is to extract the page-private widgets from `expenses_page.dart` into separate files in `presentation/widgets/` as well, so the page file becomes even slimmer.

Extracted the reusable `expenses_page` pieces into separate widget files and kept [`ExpensesPage`](d:/Dev/FlutterProjects/spend_wise/lib/features/expenses/presentation/pages/expenses_page.dart) as a thin composition layer.

Added:
- [`ExpensesStateView`](d:/Dev/FlutterProjects/spend_wise/lib/features/expenses/presentation/widgets/expenses_state_view.dart)
- [`ExpensesListView`](d:/Dev/FlutterProjects/spend_wise/lib/features/expenses/presentation/widgets/expenses_list_view.dart)
- [`ExpensesFeedbackView`](d:/Dev/FlutterProjects/spend_wise/lib/features/expenses/presentation/widgets/expenses_feedback_view.dart)

What changed in the page:
- `ExpensesPage` now handles only scaffold and navigation to add expense
- `_ExpensesPageBody` handles layout shell and padding
- state-specific rendering moved out to `ExpensesStateView`

Why this is better:
- `pages/` stays focused on screen composition
- `widgets/` now holds reusable presentation pieces
- the state handling logic is easier to test and reason about
- the page file is much smaller and cleaner

I also fixed a small syntax issue after extraction so the page structure is valid again.

If you want, the next cleanup step is to extract `_ExpensesPageBody` too, or even create a shared responsive page wrapper since the same centered constrained layout is already appearing in multiple screens.

# Context from my IDE setup:

## Active file: lib/features/expenses/presentation/cubit/expense_cubit.dart

- injection_container.dart: lib/core/di/injection_container.dart

## My request for Codex:
Act as a senior Flutter engineer and refactor this ExpenseCubit to improve architecture, scalability, and code quality.

Goals:

* Follow clean architecture principles strictly
* Keep Cubit focused on state management only

Required changes:

1. Remove business logic from Cubit:

   * Do NOT parse strings (e.g. double.parse) inside Cubit
   * Do NOT generate IDs inside Cubit
   * Cubit should receive already validated and formatted data

2. Improve code reuse:

   * Extract repeated logic (like reloading expenses) into a private method

3. Improve performance:

   * Avoid reloading all expenses after every operation
   * Use optimistic updates where possible (update local state instead of calling getExpenses every time)

4. Improve error handling:

   * Replace catch (_) with proper error handling
   * Use meaningful error messages (use exception message if possible)

5. Improve readability:

   * Clean up method structure
   * Keep methods small and focused

6. Keep API clean:

   * Methods like addExpense/updateExpense should accept proper types (e.g. double amount, not String)

7. (Optional but preferred):

   * Suggest improvements for state (e.g. using Equatable or better state modeling)

Output:

* Refactored ExpenseCubit code
* Short explanation of improvements and why they matter


</details>

Refactored [`ExpenseCubit`](d:/Dev/FlutterProjects/spend_wise/lib/features/expenses/presentation/cubit/expense_cubit.dart) so it now behaves like a proper presentation-layer state manager.

Key changes:
- `addExpense` and `updateExpense` now accept an `Expense` entity instead of raw strings.
- Removed `double.parse`, `trim`, and ID generation from the Cubit.
- Extracted repeated submission flow into `_performSubmission(...)`.
- Extracted fetching into `_fetchExpenses()` and load success into `_emitLoadSuccess(...)`.
- Replaced full reload-after-write with optimistic local state updates:
  - add: append to state list
  - update: replace matching item
  - delete: remove matching item
- Replaced broad `catch (_)``-style handling with `catch (error, stackTrace)` plus `addError(...)`.
- Added `_mapErrorToMessage(...)` so errors shown to the UI are cleaner and more meaningful.

To keep the app compiling with the cleaner Cubit API, I also updated:
- [`ExpenseForm`](d:/Dev/FlutterProjects/spend_wise/lib/features/expenses/presentation/widgets/expense_form.dart) to build an `Expense` before submission
- [`ExpenseFormPage`](d:/Dev/FlutterProjects/spend_wise/lib/features/expenses/presentation/pages/expense_form_page.dart) to pass `Expense` objects to the Cubit

Why this matters:
- The Cubit is now focused on state transitions, not business/data formatting.
- The API is cleaner and easier to test.
- Optimistic updates avoid unnecessary reads after every mutation.
- Error handling is more production-friendly.
- The private helpers make the code easier to extend when you add more expense operations later.

One architectural note: ID generation is no longer in the Cubit, but it’s still happening in the form widget right now. A stronger next step would be moving that into a dedicated ID generator service or create-expense use case so even the UI doesn’t own it.

Optional state improvement:
- `ExpenseState` would benefit from `Equatable` for cleaner rebuild comparisons and more predictable testing.
- Longer term, you could also model load state and submission state as separate sealed state objects if the feature grows more complex.

  * presentation
  * domain
  * data

* No data parsing inside Cubit

  * Bad practices

  * Folder structure

  * Reusability
* Remove duplicated code
* Apply SOLID principles

## 3. Cubit Improvements

* Ensure:

  * Proper state management
  * No unnecessary emits
  * Optimistic updates where applicable
  * Clean error handling
* Remove any logic that belongs to UseCases

## 4. UI Refactor (IMPORTANT)

* Convert ALL StatefulWidgets → StatelessWidgets
* Move all logic to Cubit
* Split large widgets into smaller reusable widgets
* Replace setState with BlocBuilder / BlocListener
* Improve readability and structure

* Avoid unnecessary rebuilds
* Use const constructors where possible

```
import 'package:spend_wise/features/categories/domain/repositories/category_repository.dart';

class CanDeleteCategory {
  const CanDeleteCategory(this._categoryRepository);

  final CategoryRepository _categoryRepository;

  Future<bool> call(String categoryId) async {
    final categories = await _categoryRepository.getCategories();
    final category = categories.where((c) => c.id == categoryId).firstOrNull;

    if (category == null) {
      return false;
    }

    return !category.isDefault;
  }
}
```

```
class CategoryModel {

    required this.id,
    required this.name,
    required this.icon,
    required this.color,
    required this.isDefault,
    required this.createdAt,
  });

  factory CategoryModel.fromJson(Map<String, dynamic> json) =>
      _$CategoryModelFromJson(json);

  factory CategoryModel.fromEntity(Category category) {
    return CategoryModel(
      id: category.id,
      name: category.name,
      icon: category.icon,
      color: category.color,
```

```
import 'package:spend_wise/features/categories/data/datasources/category_local_data_source.dart';
import 'package:spend_wise/features/categories/data/models/category_model.dart';
import 'package:spend_wise/features/categories/domain/entities/category.dart';

class CategoryRepositoryImpl implements CategoryRepository {
  const CategoryRepositoryImpl(this._localDataSource);

  final CategoryLocalDataSource _localDataSource;

  @override
  Future<void> addCategory(Category category) {
    final categoryModel = CategoryModel.fromEntity(category);
    return _localDataSource.addCategory(categoryModel);
  }

  @override
  Future<void> deleteCategory(String id) {
    return _localDataSource.deleteCategory(id);
  }

  @override
  Future<List<Category>> getCategories() {
    return _localDataSource.getCategories().then((categoryModels) 
...(truncated)
```

</details>

I’ve finished the review pass, and there are a few concrete issues we should fix before calling this feature production-ready:

1. `StatefulWidget` + `setState` is carrying form logic in `CategoryForm`, `IconPicker`, `ColorPicker`, `CategoryFormPage`, and `CategoryListPage`.
2. The Cubit contains validation/business rules in `_validateCategory`, which belongs outside presentation.
3. ID generation happens inside the form widget, which tightly couples UI to entity creation.
4. The same icon-name-to-`IconData` mapping is duplicated in multiple widgets.
5. `CategoryListPage` shows success UI for delete before the delete operation actually succeeds.
6. The current state model mixes load status, delete status, form submission status, and transient error handling in a way that causes awkward emits and manual `clearError()`.
7. There’s route-path inconsistency: categories imports `config/routes/route_names.dart`, while other features are using `app/routes/...`.
8. `CanDeleteCategory` exists in domain but isn’t being used where it matters.

I’m going to refactor this step by step with minimal churn: first centralize shared category presentation metadata, then clean up Cubit/state, then convert the form/list UI to stateless Bloc-driven widgets.

I’ve got the review findings translated into a concrete refactor plan. The biggest structural improvement is sharing one `CategoryCubit` between the list and form flows, because that lets us remove a lot of fragile reload/navigation behavior and make updates feel instant.

<details>
<summary>Tool: <code>apply_patch</code></summary>

**Review**

I found these main issues in the original categories feature:

- `StatefulWidget` + `setState` was doing form and picker state in UI.
  Files like [`category_form.dart`](d:/Dev/FlutterProjects/spend_wise/lib/features/categories/presentation/widgets/category_form.dart), [`icon_picker.dart`](d:/Dev/FlutterProjects/spend_wise/lib/features/categories/presentation/widgets/icon_picker.dart), [`color_picker.dart`](d:/Dev/FlutterProjects/spend_wise/lib/features/categories/presentation/widgets/color_picker.dart), [`category_form_page.dart`](d:/Dev/FlutterProjects/spend_wise/lib/features/categories/presentation/pages/category_form_page.dart), and [`category_list_page.dart`](d:/Dev/FlutterProjects/spend_wise/lib/features/categories/presentation/pages/category_list_page.dart) were holding UI state and workflow logic together.

- The Cubit had validation/business rules mixed into presentation logic.
  The old `CategoryCubit` validated category name and deletion rules directly while also coordinating UI flags and side effects.

- Entity creation was happening in the form widget.
  That couples the UI to domain construction and makes the feature harder to test and evolve.

- Icon metadata was duplicated.
  The icon-name-to-`IconData` mapping existed in multiple widgets, which is a maintenance smell and violates DRY.

- Navigation created separate Cubits for list and form flows.
  That can easily lead to stale list state after add/edit operations.

- Error/success handling was awkward.
  The previous state model mixed loading, delete, add/update, and transient errors in a way that required manual cleanup like `clearError()`.

**Refactor**

I refactored the feature around those problems:

- Added shared presentation metadata in [`category_presentation_data.dart`](d:/Dev/FlutterProjects/spend_wise/lib/features/categories/presentation/utils/category_presentation_data.dart) so icons/colors are defined once and reused everywhere.
- Refactored [`CategoryCubit`](d:/Dev/FlutterProjects/spend_wise/lib/features/categories/presentation/cubit/category_cubit.dart) and [`CategoryState`](d:/Dev/FlutterProjects/spend_wise/lib/features/categories/presentation/cubit/category_state.dart) so the Cubit now owns:
  - form state
  - submission state
  - deletion state
  - load state
  - success/error messages
- Converted the form and picker UI to Bloc-driven stateless widgets:
  - [`category_form.dart`](d:/Dev/FlutterProjects/spend_wise/lib/features/categories/presentation/widgets/category_form.dart)
  - [`icon_picker.dart`](d:/Dev/FlutterProjects/spend_wise/lib/features/categories/presentation/widgets/icon_picker.dart)
  - [`color_picker.dart`](d:/Dev/FlutterProjects/spend_wise/lib/features/categories/presentation/widgets/color_picker.dart)
- Refactored pages to be thinner and more declarative:
  - [`category_form_page.dart`](d:/Dev/FlutterProjects/spend_wise/lib/features/categories/presentation/pages/category_form_page.dart)
  - [`category_list_page.dart`](d:/Dev/FlutterProjects/spend_wise/lib/features/categories/presentation/pages/category_list_page.dart)
- Updated DI in [`injection_container.dart`](d:/Dev/FlutterProjects/spend_wise/lib/core/di/injection_container.dart) so `CategoryCubit` also receives `CanDeleteCategory`.
- Updated routing in [`app_router.dart`](d:/Dev/FlutterProjects/spend_wise/lib/config/routes/app_router.dart) so standalone category form routes initialize form state properly.

**Before vs After**

- Before: duplicated icon/color config in multiple widgets.
  After: one shared source of truth.

- Before: UI owned form state and called `setState`.
  After: Cubit owns form state, UI is Bloc-driven.

- Before: list and form flows were loosely coordinated.
  After: list-to-form navigation reuses the same Cubit instance for a cleaner optimistic flow.

- Before: success/error handling relied on broad state flags and manual clearing.
  After: load/submission/deletion concerns are separated in state.

- Before: feature widgets were tightly coupled and harder to test.
  After: responsibilities are cleaner and more reusable.

One note: I wasn’t able to complete a full analyzer run because the command was interrupted, so I’d still run `dart analyze` or `flutter analyze` locally to catch any remaining compile-time drift.

```
import 'package:spend_wise/core/base/requests_status.dart';
import 'package:spend_wise/features/categories/domain/entities/category.dart';
```

```
class CategoryState {
  final RequestsStatus categoriesStatus;
  final RequestsStatus submissionStatus;
```

I refactored [`CategoryCubit`](d:/Dev/FlutterProjects/spend_wise/lib/features/categories/presentation/cubit/category_cubit.dart) and tightened [`CategoryState`](d:/Dev/FlutterProjects/spend_wise/lib/features/categories/presentation/cubit/category_state.dart) around cleaner state management.

What improved:
- Proper state management:
  - `CategoryState` is now `const`
  - load, submit, and delete flows stay separated with `categoriesStatus`, `submissionStatus`, and `deletionStatus`
- No unnecessary emits:
  - `updateCategoryName`, `selectIcon`, and `selectColor` now return early if the value didn’t change
  - `loadCategories()` skips if already loading
  - `clearMessages()` skips if there’s nothing to clear
  - `_emitLoadSuccess()` avoids re-emitting unchanged category lists
- Optimistic updates:
  - add/update/delete now update local state directly with `_appendCategory`, `_replaceCategory`, and `_removeCategory`
  - no full reload after every mutation
- Clean error handling:
  - all async paths use `catch (error, stackTrace)` with `addError(...)`
  - error messages go through `_mapErrorToMessage(...)`
  - submission and deletion errors are emitted through dedicated helpers
- Better structure:
  - repeated action flow moved into `_performSubmission(...)`
  - repeated emit logic moved into `_emitLoadSuccess`, `_emitSubmissionError`, `_emitDeletionError`

One important note: the Cubit is cleaner now, but it still builds a `Category` and generates IDs in `_buildCategoryFromState()`. If you want the strictest clean-architecture version, the next step is to move that into a dedicated use case or factory so the Cubit receives a ready-to-save domain object instead of constructing one itself.

I finished the category UI refactor around the goals you listed.

What changed:
- All category presentation widgets are stateless now.
- Form/page logic stays Cubit-driven through `BlocBuilder` and `BlocListener`.
- I split the larger UI into smaller reusable widgets:
  - [`CategoryFeedbackView`](d:/Dev/FlutterProjects/spend_wise/lib/features/categories/presentation/widgets/category_feedback_view.dart)
  - [`CategoryLoadingOverlay`](d:/Dev/FlutterProjects/spend_wise/lib/features/categories/presentation/widgets/category_loading_overlay.dart)
  - [`CategoryPreviewCard`](d:/Dev/FlutterProjects/spend_wise/lib/features/categories/presentation/widgets/category_preview_card.dart)
  - [`CategoryNameField`](d:/Dev/FlutterProjects/spend_wise/lib/features/categories/presentation/widgets/category_name_field.dart)
  - [`CategorySubmitButton`](d:/Dev/FlutterProjects/spend_wise/lib/features/categories/presentation/widgets/category_submit_button.dart)

Refactored files:
- [`category_form.dart`](d:/Dev/FlutterProjects/spend_wise/lib/features/categories/presentation/widgets/category_form.dart)
- [`category_form_page.dart`](d:/Dev/FlutterProjects/spend_wise/lib/features/categories/presentation/pages/category_form_page.dart)
- [`category_list_page.dart`](d:/Dev/FlutterProjects/spend_wise/lib/features/categories/presentation/pages/category_list_page.dart)

Why this is better:
- The page files are thinner and easier to read.
- Reusable UI pieces are now isolated in `widgets/`.
- Loading/error/empty states are more consistent.
- Deletion now shows a dedicated loading overlay instead of silently blocking.
- The preview card has small built-in animations for a better feel without adding complexity.
- Rebuild scope is smaller because the UI is split into focused widgets instead of one large tree.

On DI: your categories setup already follows the correct shape in [`injection_container.dart`](d:/Dev/FlutterProjects/spend_wise/lib/core/di/injection_container.dart):
- `factory` for `CategoryCubit`
- `lazySingleton` for use cases and repository
- `singleton` for Hive box

One note: I didn’t run a full analyzer pass after this last UI split, so I’d still run `flutter analyze` locally to catch any remaining compile-time drift.

## Codex <sup>5/1/2026, 2:20:44 PM</sup>

For this app, the best structure is usually:

1. One top-level app shell
2. Feature pages routed inside it
3. A simple primary navigation pattern
4. Local feature navigation for create/edit/detail flows

For your expense/subscription tracker, I would not use a sidebar as the main pattern. On mobile, the best default is a `BottomNavigationBar` or Material 3 `NavigationBar`.

**Best option for this app**

Use a persistent bottom navigation with 4 main sections:
- `Dashboard`
- `Expenses`
- `Subscriptions`
- `Categories`

Then keep secondary screens as pushed routes:
- `Add/Edit Expense`
- `Add/Edit Category`
- `Add/Edit Subscription`
- maybe `Settings`

That gives you:
- fast access to the main areas
- clean mental model for users
- scalable structure as features grow
- simpler route handling than mixing everything into drawers and nested stacks

**Why not a sidebar first**
- A drawer/sidebar is weaker for frequent switching between core sections
- This app is action-heavy, not admin-panel-heavy
- Bottom nav is more natural for mobile finance apps

A drawer can still be added later for less frequent pages like:
- `Settings`
- `Backup / Sync`
- `About`
- `Export`

**Recommended app structure**

```text
lib/
├── app/
│   ├── app.dart
│   ├── shell/
│   │   └── main_shell.dart
│   ├── routes/
│   │   ├── app_router.dart
│   │   └── route_names.dart
│   └── navigation/
│       └── app_destinations.dart
├── features/
│   ├── dashboard/
│   ├── expenses/
│   ├── subscriptions/
│   ├── categories/
│   └── settings/
```

**How pages link together**

Think in two layers:

**1. Global navigation**
Handled by the shell:
- tapping bottom nav switches top-level sections
- each tab shows its main page

Example:
- `DashboardPage`
- `ExpensesPage`
- `SubscriptionsPage`
- `CategoryListPage`

**2. Local flow navigation**
Handled by pushed routes:
- from `ExpensesPage` -> `ExpenseFormPage`
- from `CategoryListPage` -> `CategoryFormPage`

So:
- main sections = bottom nav
- forms/details = route push

**What the shell should do**

Create a `MainShellPage` with:
- `Scaffold`
- body showing the selected tab
- bottom navigation bar
- optional FAB that changes by tab

Example behavior:
- On `Expenses`, FAB = add expense
- On `Categories`, FAB = add category
- On `Subscriptions`, FAB = add subscription

That feels much cleaner than each top-level page inventing its own app frame.

**AppBar guidance**
Use a normal `AppBar` per section:
- `Dashboard`
- `Expenses`
- `Subscriptions`
- `Categories`

Keep the title simple.
Add lightweight actions only where useful:
- search later
- filter
- sort
- sync status

**My recommendation for your app**
Use this navigation model:

- Bottom navigation for:
  - Dashboard
  - Expenses
  - Subscriptions
  - Categories

- Drawer only for:
  - Settings
  - Sync / Backup
  - About

- Push routes for:
  - add/edit forms
  - details
  - analytics subpages

**Routing style**
Your current [`app_router.dart`](d:/Dev/FlutterProjects/spend_wise/lib/config/routes/app_router.dart) is fine as a starting point, but as the app grows, I’d structure routes into:
- shell routes
- feature form/detail routes
- shared route names

Example route groups:
```dart
/dashboard
/expenses
/expenses/form
/subscriptions
/subscriptions/form
/categories
/categories/form
/settings
```

**Best long-term pattern**
If you want production-ready scalability:
- keep `AppRouter` as the central route entry
- add a `MainShellPage`
- make each feature expose its own page entry points
- keep Cubits feature-scoped, not global unless necessary

**Short answer**
The best option for this app is:
- `NavigationBar` at the bottom for main sections
- `AppBar` at the top for section context
- pushed routes for forms and details
- optional drawer for low-frequency pages like settings/sync

If you want, I can build the `MainShellPage` and refactor your current routes so the app has proper real navigation starting now.

```
import 'package:flutter/material.dart';
import 'package:flutter_bloc/flutter_bloc.dart';
import 'package:flutter_screenutil/flutter_screenutil.dart';

import '../../../../core/base/requests_status.dart';
import '../../domain/entities/expense.dart';
import '../cubit/expense_cubit.dart';
import '../cubit/expense_state.dart';
import '../widgets/expense_form.dart';

class ExpenseFormPage extends StatelessWidget {
  const ExpenseFormPage({super.key, this.expense});

  final Expense? expense;

  @override
  Widget build(BuildContext context) {
    final isEditing = expense != null;

    return BlocListener<ExpenseCubit, ExpenseState>(
      listenWhen: (previous, current) =>
          previous.submissionStatus != current.submissionStatus,
      listener: (context, state) {
        if (state.submissionStatus == RequestsStatus.success) {
```

I started the app structure by adding a real navigation shell so your pages can be linked together in a production-friendly way.

What I added:
- [`MainShellPage`](d:/Dev/FlutterProjects/spend_wise/lib/app/shell/main_shell_page.dart)
- [`SettingsPage`](d:/Dev/FlutterProjects/spend_wise/lib/features/settings/presentation/pages/settings_page.dart)

What changed:
- [`route_names.dart`](d:/Dev/FlutterProjects/spend_wise/lib/config/routes/route_names.dart)
  - added `/` as `mainShellPage`
  - added `settingsPage`
- [`app_router.dart`](d:/Dev/FlutterProjects/spend_wise/lib/config/routes/app_router.dart)
  - now routes into the shell
  - provides shared `ExpenseCubit` and `CategoryCubit` at shell level
- [`spend_wise_app.dart`](d:/Dev/FlutterProjects/spend_wise/lib/spend_wise_app.dart)
  - now starts from `RouteNames.mainShellPage`
- [`ExpensesPage`](d:/Dev/FlutterProjects/spend_wise/lib/features/expenses/presentation/pages/expenses_page.dart)
  - now supports `showScaffold: false` so it can be embedded inside the shell
  - opens the add-expense form using the existing Cubit instance
- [`CategoryListPage`](d:/Dev/FlutterProjects/spend_wise/lib/features/categories/presentation/pages/category_list_page.dart)
  - now supports `showScaffold: false`
  - exposes reusable `openFormPage(...)` and delete confirmation helpers for shell use

Navigation structure now:
- Bottom navigation for:
  - Dashboard
  - Expenses
  - Subscriptions
  - Categories
- Drawer for:
  - Settings
  - About
- Push routes for:
  - Add/Edit Expense
  - Add/Edit Category

Why this is the right direction:
- Main sections are now consistently reachable from one shell
- Feature Cubits are shared at the shell level, so list/form flows stay connected
- Forms open as secondary flows instead of pretending to be top-level destinations
- The app is now ready to grow without every feature inventing its own navigation frame

A couple of sections are placeholders for now:
- Dashboard
- Subscriptions
- Settings is a simple starter page

So the next natural step is:
1. Build the real `DashboardPage`
2. Build the real `SubscriptionsPage`
3. Optionally add a dynamic FAB policy per tab with richer actions

I didn’t run a full analyzer pass, so you should still run `flutter analyze` locally after this shell refactor.

عدلتها في [`main_shell_page.dart`](d:/Dev/FlutterProjects/spend_wise/lib/config/shell/main_shell_page.dart) بحيث صار التحديد واضحًا على النص والأيقونة معًا.

الذي تغير:
- أضفت `NavigationBarTheme`
- خصصت `labelTextStyle` للحالة المختارة وغير المختارة
- خصصت `iconTheme` للحالة المختارة وغير المختارة
- فعلت `labelBehavior: NavigationDestinationLabelBehavior.alwaysShow`
- خليت لون المختار من `colorScheme.primary` وغير المختار من `onSurfaceVariant`

النتيجة:
- الصفحة المختارة يظهر نصها بلون أوضح ووزن أثقل
- الأيقونة والنص الآن متناسقان في حالة التحديد
- الصفحات غير المختارة تظل ظاهرة لكن بشكل أهدأ

إذا تريد، أقدر أعملها أوضح أكثر بإحدى طريقتين:
- نخلي خلفية التبويب المختار أكبر وأبرز
- أو نخلي النص المختار بحجم أكبر قليلًا مع أنيميشن ناعم عند التبديل

Refactored [`main_shell_page.dart`](d:/Dev/FlutterProjects/spend_wise/lib/config/shell/main_shell_page.dart) into smaller, clearer pieces without changing behavior.

What I split out:
- [`ShellDestination`](d:/Dev/FlutterProjects/spend_wise/lib/config/shell/models/shell_destination.dart)
- [`MainShellDrawer`](d:/Dev/FlutterProjects/spend_wise/lib/config/shell/widgets/main_shell_drawer.dart)
- [`MainShellNavigationBar`](d:/Dev/FlutterProjects/spend_wise/lib/config/shell/widgets/main_shell_navigation_bar.dart)
- [`ShellPlaceholderPage`](d:/Dev/FlutterProjects/spend_wise/lib/config/shell/widgets/shell_placeholder_page.dart)
- [`buildShellDestinations()`](d:/Dev/FlutterProjects/spend_wise/lib/config/shell/widgets/shell_destinations.dart)

Now the main file is responsible فقط عن:
- current selected tab
- loading initial feature data
- composing the shell scaffold

Why this is better:
- `MainShellPage` صار أخف وأسهل للقراءة
- كل جزء له مسؤولية واحدة واضحة
- تعديل الـ bottom nav أو drawer أو destinations لاحقًا صار أسهل بكثير
- إضافة tabs جديدة لاحقًا ستكون من خلال ملف الوجهات فقط بدل لمس الصفحة الرئيسية كلها

إذا تريد، الخطوة التالية المنطقية هي:
- تحويل `_currentIndex` أيضًا إلى Cubit صغير خاص بالـ shell
- أو إضافة دعم deep linking بحيث يفتح التطبيق مباشرة على tab معيّن أو form معيّن

  - سجلت `ShellCubit` كـ `factory`

لماذا هذا أفضل:
- حالة الـ shell أصبحت خارج الواجهة وداخل Cubit واضح ومخصص
- الصفحة نفسها أصبحت أنظف وأسهل للقراءة والاختبار

- لاحقًا سيسهل جدًا إضافة:
  - حفظ آخر tab مفتوح
  - deep linking إلى tab معين
  - ربط الـ shell مع auth أو permissions

- `ShellCubit` الآن يدير فقط `currentIndex` وهذا ممتاز كبداية.
- لو أردت، الخطوة التالية أقدر أعملها هي:
  - نقل `buildShellDestinations()` إلى طبقة أنظف مرتبطة بالـ shell state
  - أو إضافة `goToExpenses() / goToCategories()` methods داخل `ShellCubit` لقراءة أوضح في المشروع.

---

## Codex <sup>5/2/2026, 11:54:27 AM</sup>

Yes, `shell` is a good name here. `MainShellPage` is also a good name.

But `config` is not the best place for it.

For this kind of file, `shell` is part of app structure/navigation, not app configuration. `config` usually feels better for things like:
- themes
- env values
- constants
- route definitions
- flavor setup

A shell page is really a UI composition layer, so a better place is usually one of these:

- `lib/app/shell/`
- `lib/app/navigation/`
- `lib/app/layout/`

My recommendation:
- move `MainShellPage` and related shell widgets to `lib/app/shell/`
- keep route files in `lib/app/routes/` or `lib/config/routes/` if you prefer
- keep true config-only files in `config`

Best structure for your case:

```text
lib/
├── app/
│   ├── shell/
│   │   ├── main_shell_page.dart
│   │   ├── cubit/
│   │   │   ├── shell_cubit.dart
│   │   │   └── shell_state.dart
│   │   ├── models/
│   │   │   └── shell_destination.dart
│   │   └── widgets/
│   │       ├── main_shell_drawer.dart
│   │       ├── main_shell_navigation_bar.dart
│   │       ├── shell_destinations.dart
│   │       └── shell_placeholder_page.dart
│   └── routes/
│       ├── app_router.dart
│       └── route_names.dart
```

Naming notes:
- `shell` = good
- `main_shell_page.dart` = good
- `shell_destination.dart` = good
- `config/shell` = not ideal
- `config/routes` = acceptable, but `app/routes` is cleaner

So short answer:
- `shell` name: yes, good
- `MainShellPage`: yes, good
- putting it under `config`: not ideal
- better place: `app/shell`

If you want, I can move the whole shell structure from `lib/config/shell/` to `lib/app/shell/` and update imports cleanly.
